Definitions Without Causes: The Fifth Type and Rasm as a Sixth
Author presents the fifth type of definition for uncaused entities and introduces rasm as a sixth aspect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify definitions of simple entities (like point and unity) and distinguish them from descriptions (rasm).

Core Idea
Some terms have no essential causes and must be defined by their meaning alone; rasm provides a non-essential distinguishing description.

The author concludes by discussing definitions of simple entities that have no causes, such as 'point' and 'unity', and then mentions that 'rasm' (description) can serve as a sixth type of definition. This lesson clarifies how to handle definitions where causal analysis is impossible, and when description substitutes for real definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify simple entities
Things without causes, e.g., point, unity, and definition itself. Their definition does not rely on causation.
Simple entities are indivisible or primary concepts.
2
Understand why their definitions are not causal
They have no essential cause; their definition is a direct statement of meaning. For example, 'unity' is defined, but it has no cause.
This differs from the first type (nominal) because it captures the quiddity.
3
Distinguish this from the first type (nominal)
The fifth type is not merely a verbal explanation; it is a real definition of a simple essence, but not derived from demonstration.
The author says it is not just 'sharh al-ism'.
4
Learn about rasm
Rasm is a description that distinguishes a thing without capturing its essence. It is sometimes called 'hadd' loosely, making a sixth type.
Rasm is used when a real definition is not possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحد يطلق بالتشكيك على خمسة : الأول : الحدّ الشارح لمعنى الاسم، ولا يلتفت فيه إلى وجود الشيء وعدمه، بل ربما يكون مشكوكاً. ونذكر الحدّ ثم إن ظهر وجوده عرف أن الحد لم يكن بحسب الاسم المجرد وشرحه بل هو عنوان الذات وشرحه . الثاني : بحسب الذات وهو نتيجة برهان . والثالث : ما هو بحسب الذات وهو مبدأ برهان . والرابع : ما هو بحسب الذات. والحدّ التام الجامع لما هو مبدأ برهان ونتيجة برهان، كما إذا سُئلت عن حدّ الكُسوف فقلت : امحاء ضوء القمر لتوسط الأرض بينه وبين الشمس، فامحاءُ ضوء القمر هو نتيجة برهان وتوسط الأرض المبدأ، فإنك في معرض البرهان تقول : متى توسطت الأرض فانمحى النور فيكون التوسط حدا أوسط فهو مبدأ برهان وإلَّا انمحى حد أكبر فهو نتيجة برهان. ولذلك يتداخل البرهان والحد فإن العلل الذاتية من هذا الجنس تدخل في حدود الأشياء كما تدخل في براهينها فكل ما له علة فلا بد من ذكر علته الذاتية في حده لتتم صورة ذاته، وقد تدخل العلل الأربعة في حدّ الشيء الذي له العلل الأربعة كقوله في حد القادوم : إنه آلة صناعية من حديد، شكله كذا يقطع به الخشب نحتاً؛ فقولك : آلة جنس وصناعية تدلّ على المبدأ الفاعل، والشكل يدلّ على الصورة، والحديد يدلّ على المادة والنحت على الغاية، وبه الاحتراز عن المثقب والمنشار إذ لا ينحت بهما. وقد يقتصر في الحدّ على نتيجة البرهان إذا حصل التمييز بها فيقال: حدّ الكسوف انمحاء ضوء القمر، فيسمى هذا حدا نتيجة برهان وإن اقتصر على العلّة وقال : الكسوف هو توسط الأرض بين القمر وبين الشمس، وحصل به التمييز قيل حدّ مبدأ برهان والحد التام المركب منهما . الخامس : ما هو حدّ لأمور ليس لها علل وأسباب ولو كان لها علل لكانت عللها غير داخلة في جواهرها كتحديد النقطة والوحدة والحدّ ، فإن الوحدة يذكر لها تعريف وليس للوحدة سبب، والحدّ يحدّ فإنه قول دالّ على ماهية الشيء، وللقول فإنه حادث لا محالة لعلّة لكن مُسبِّبه ليس ذاتياً له كانمحاء ضوء القمر في الكسوف، فهذا الخامس ليس بمجرّد شرح الاسم فقط، ولا هو مبدأ برهان ولا نتيجة برهان ولا هو مركب منهما ؛ فهذه أقسام ما يطلق عليه اسم الحد، وقد يُسمّى الرسم حدا على أنه مميز فيكون ذلك وجهاً سادساً .
And 'definition' is predicated by tashkik upon five: First: the definition that explains the meaning of the name, without regard to the existence or non-existence of the thing; indeed it may be doubtful. We mention the definition, then if its existence appears, it is known that the definition was not according to the mere name and its explanation, but rather it is the designation of the essence and its explanation. Second: according to the essence, and it is the result of a demonstration. Third: what is according to the essence, and it is the principle of a demonstration. Fourth: what is according to the essence, and it is the complete definition combining what is the principle of a demonstration and the result of a demonstration, as when you are asked about the definition of eclipse and you say: 'the obliteration of the moon's light due to the interposition of the earth between it and the sun'. So the obliteration of the moon's light is the result of a demonstration, and the interposition of the earth is the principle. For in the context of demonstration you say: whenever the earth interposes, then the light is obliterated. So the interposition becomes the middle term, which is the principle of the demonstration, and the obliteration becomes the major term, which is the result. Therefore demonstration and definition overlap; for essential causes of this kind enter into the definitions of things as they enter into their demonstrations. So everything that has a cause must have its essential cause mentioned in its definition to complete the image of its essence. And the four causes may enter into the definition of a thing that has four causes, as in the definition of an adze: it is an artificial tool made of iron, shaped in such a way, used to cut wood by carving. So your saying 'tool' is the genus, 'artificial' indicates the efficient cause, 'shape' indicates the formal cause, 'iron' indicates the material cause, and 'carving' indicates the final cause; and by this it is distinguished from the awl and the saw, for they are not used for carving. And sometimes one may confine the definition to the result of the demonstration if distinction is obtained by it: it is said 'the definition of eclipse is the obliteration of the moon's light', and this is called a definition as the result of demonstration. If one confines it to the cause and says 'the eclipse is the interposition of the earth between the moon and the sun', and distinction is obtained, it is called a definition as the principle of demonstration. And the complete definition is composed of both. Fifth: what is a definition for things that have no causes and reasons; and if they had causes, their causes would not be included in their essences, like the definition of point, unity, and definition itself. For unity has a definition given for it, but unity has no cause. And definition is defined: it is a statement indicating the quiddity of a thing. But the statement is necessarily originated, and has a cause, but its efficient cause is not essential to it, like the obliteration of the moon's light in the eclipse. So this fifth is not merely an explanation of the name, nor is it a principle of demonstration nor a result of demonstration nor composed of both. These are the divisions of what is called definition. And 'description' (rasm) may be called a definition, as it is a distinguisher, so that would be a sixth aspect.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This chapter enumerates the five types of definition (hadd) explained by tashkik (graded predication). The first type is a nominal definition that clarifies the meaning of a term without assuming the thing's existence; it is essentially a lexical explanation. The second type is a definition that is the conclusion of a demonstration (natijat burhan), i.e., the definiendum's essence is known via a proof. The third type is the definition that serves as the premise (mabda' burhan) of a demonstration, i.e., the essential cause. The fourth type combines both: it includes both the cause and the effect, as in the definition of a lunar eclipse stating both the interposition of the earth (cause) and the obliteration of light (effect). The author explains that demonstration and definition merge here because essential causes are part of both. He further illustrates how the four causes (material, formal, efficient, final) can all enter a definition, using the example of an adze (qadum). The definition mentions genus (tool), matter (iron), form (shape), agent (artificial), and purpose (carving). This distinguishes the adze from other tools. The fifth type is for simple entities that have no causes (like point, unity, and definition itself). Such definitions are not merely nominal nor derived from demonstration. The chapter ends by noting that 'description' (rasm) is sometimes called a definition, making a sixth kind.

Key Terms
النقطة
الوحدة
الحد
الرسم

C) Unity
D) Tool

Key Takeaway
The fifth type of definition is for uncaused simple entities; rasm is a description that can serve as a definition in a loose sense.

The Four Causes in Definition: The Adze Example
Author defines adze using the four causes to illustrate how causes enter definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four causes (material, formal, efficient, final) in a definition and construct a definition of an Islamic legal term using the four causes.

Core Idea
A complete definition includes all four causes, not just genus and differentia.

The author explains that demonstration and definition overlap because both involve essential causes. To illustrate, he gives the definition of an adze, showing how each of the four causes corresponds to a part of the definition. Understanding this helps you see how definitions in Islamic sciences often incorporate causal elements, making them more precise and connected to demonstrative reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The author defines 'adze' (القادوم). Locate the definiendum in the Arabic passage. It is a manufactured tool used for carving wood.
The adze is a concrete example from craftsmanship.
2
Extract the genus
The genus (جنس) is 'tool' (آلة). The author explicitly says 'your saying tool is genus'.
3
Identify the differentia and map to causes
The differentia includes 'manufactured' (efficient cause), 'shape' (formal cause), 'iron' (material cause), and 'carving' (final cause). Each part of the definition points to one of the four Aristotelian causes.
Notice that the differentia here is composite, not a single element.
4
Verify the definition distinguishes the thing
The author notes that by including 'carving' (the final cause), the definition excludes tools like awl and saw, which are not used for carving.
This check ensures the definition is not too broad or too narrow.
5
Generalize the pattern to an Islamic concept
Think of a concept from fiqh, such as 'salah' or 'zakat'. Could you define it by listing its four causes? For example, the efficient cause might be the intention (niyyah), the material cause the physical actions, the formal cause the specific sequence, and the final cause the attainment of taqwa.
This exercise trains you to think definitionally in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Demonstration and definition overlap, for essential causes of this kind enter into the definitions of things as they enter into their demonstrations. So everything that has a cause, it is necessary to mention its essential cause in its definition to complete the form of its essence. And the four causes may enter into the definition of a thing that has four causes, as in defining an adze: it is a manufactured tool made of iron, shaped such that wood is cut with it by carving. So your saying 'tool' is genus, 'manufactured' indicates the efficient principle, 'shape' indicates form, 'iron' indicates matter, and 'carving' indicates final cause; and by this it is distinguished from the awl and the saw, for they are not used for carving. And sometimes one restricts the definition to the result of demonstration if discrimination is achieved by it, so it is said: definition of eclipse is the disappearance of the moon's light; this is called a definition by result of demonstration. And if one restricts to the cause and says: eclipse is the interposition of the earth between the moon and the sun, and discrimination is achieved, it is called a definition by principle of demonstration. And the perfect definition is composed of both. The fifth: what is a definition for things that have no causes and reasons, and if they had causes, their causes would not be included in their essences, like defining point, unity, and definition itself. For unity has a definition given for it, but unity has no cause. And definition is defined: it is a statement indicating the quiddity of a thing. And statement is necessarily originated from a cause, but its cause is not essential to it, like the disappearance of the moon's light in an eclipse. So this fifth is not merely an explanation of the name, nor is it a principle of demonstration, nor a result of demonstration, nor composed of both. These are the divisions of what is called 'definition'. And sometimes description (rasm) is called a definition as distinguisher, so that constitutes a sixth aspect.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a classification of definitions (hudud). The author begins by noting that demonstration (burhan) and definition (hadd) overlap because essential causes appear in both. He then explains the four causes (material, formal, efficient, final) using the example of defining an adze (qadum), showing how each cause corresponds to a part of the definition. He then distinguishes three types of definition based on their relation to demonstration: (1) definition as result of demonstration (e.g., eclipse as disappearance of light), (2) definition as principle of demonstration (e.g., eclipse as interposition of earth), (3) perfect definition composed of both. Then a fifth type: definition of things with no causes, like point and unity, which are defined without reference to causes. This type is not a mere name explanation nor a demonstration-based definition. Finally, he notes that description (rasm) is sometimes called a definition when it serves to distinguish, making a sixth type.

Types of Definition Based on Demonstration and Description
Author classifies definitions into five types plus description as a sixth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a given definition as a result of demonstration, a principle of demonstration, a perfect definition, a definition of a causeless thing, or a mere description (rasm).

Core Idea
Definitions vary by their relation to demonstration: some give the effect, some the cause, some both, and some apply to things with no causes.

After discussing how causes enter definitions, the author turns to a classification of definitions based on their connection to demonstration. He identifies three types directly related to demonstration (result, principle, perfect), a fifth type for things without causes, and adds a sixth through description. This classification helps you evaluate the logical structure of definitions used in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the overlap between demonstration and definition
The author begins by reiterating that essential causes appear in both demonstration and definition. This sets the stage for classifying definitions based on whether they include the cause, the effect, or both.
Recall the earlier lesson on the four causes.
2
Identify the three demonstration-related types
The author distinguishes: (1) definition as result of demonstration (حد نتيجة برهان) – gives the effect only, e.g., 'eclipse is disappearance of moon's light'; (2) definition as principle of demonstration (حد مبدأ برهان) – gives the cause only, e.g., 'eclipse is interposition of earth'; (3) perfect definition (الحد التام) – combines cause and effect, e.g., 'eclipse is interposition of earth causing disappearance of light'.
The perfect definition is the most complete.
3
Learn the fifth type: definitions of causeless things
The fifth type applies to things that have no causes, like unity (الوحدة) and point (النقطة). Their definitions do not involve causes, yet they are not mere name explanations. For example, 'unity is that which is not divisible'.
The author emphasizes that these definitions are not principles, results, or perfect.
4
Learn the sixth type: description (rasm) as definition
The author notes that sometimes a description (الرسم) is called a definition because it serves to distinguish the thing, even though it does not reveal the essence. This adds a sixth category.
Description is weaker than genuine definition.
5
Apply the classification to an Islamic example
Consider the definition of 'iman' (faith) as 'belief in the heart, statement by the tongue, and action by the limbs'. Is this a result, principle, perfect, or something else? Discuss.
This exercise builds analytical skill in evaluating definitions.

The Method of Composing a Definition (Tarkib)
Author describes the method of attaining a definition by composing genus and differentia through elimination and checking coextensiveness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a definition by composing genus and differentia, and verify that it satisfies both coextensiveness and equality in meaning.

Core Idea
A proper definition must be both coextensive with the name and fully convey the essence.

How is a definition acquired if not by demonstration? This lesson reveals the step-by-step method of composition (tarkib). By carefully selecting essential predicates and adding the differentia, you can craft a definition that is both extensionally and intensionally accurate. The author provides a rigorous procedure that Islamic scholars have used to define concepts in every science.

Guided Path
1
Collect individuals of the definiendum
Start with concrete instances of the thing to be defined, ensuring they are not further divided into sub-kinds. This grounds the definition in reality.
E.g., for defining 'human', take individual humans like Zayd and 'Amr.
2
Identify the genus from the ten categories
Determine which of Aristotle's ten categories (substance, quantity, quality, etc.) the thing belongs to. This gives the broadest genus.
For humans, the genus is substance (jawhar), specifically living body.
3
Gather all essential predicates in that genus
List all essential attributes (dhatiyyat) that constitute the essence within that genus, ignoring accidents and necessary consequences.
For a living body, essential predicates include 'body', 'growing', 'sentient', etc.
4
Eliminate redundant predicates
Remove any repeated or overlapping predicates, keeping only the nearest genus (e.g., 'animal' rather than 'body' plus 'living').
Redundancy would weaken the definition's clarity.
5
Add the differentia (fasl)
Append the attribute that distinguishes the definiendum from other species under the same genus (e.g., 'rational' for human).
The differentia completes the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : بماذا يكتسب وما طريقه؟ قلنا طريقه التركيب وهو أن نأخذ أشخاص المطلوب حده بحيث لا ينقسم، وننظر من أي جنس من جملة المقولات العشر، فنأخذ جميع المحمولات المقومة لها التي في ذلك الجنس ولا يلتفت إلى العرض واللازم بل يقتصر على المقومات ثم يحذف منها ما تكرر ويقتصر من جملتها على الأخير القريب، وتضيف إليه الفصل فإن وجدناه مساويا للمحدود من وجهين فهو الحد، ونعني بأحد الوجهين الطرد والعكس، والتساوي مع الاسم في الحمل. فمهما ثبت الحد انطلق الاسم، ومهما انطلق الاسم حصل الحد . ونعني بالوجه الثاني المساواة في المعنى، وهو أن يكون دالا على كمال حقيقة الذات لا يشد منها شيء، فكم من ذاتي متميز ترك بعض فصوله فلا يقوم ذكره في النفس صورة معقولة للمحدود مطابقة لكمال ذاته وهذا مطلوب الحدود، وقد ذكرنا وجه ذلك .
If it is said: by what is it acquired and what is its method? We say: its method is composition (tarkib), namely: we take individuals of the thing to be defined such that they are not divided, and we see from which genus among the ten categories it belongs. Then we take all the essential predicates for it that are in that genus, and we do not pay attention to accident or necessary consequence, but restrict ourselves to essentials. Then we delete from them what is repeated and restrict from the total to the nearest [genus]. Then we add the differentia to it. If we find it equal to the defined thing in two respects, then it is the definition. By one of the two respects we mean coextensiveness (tard wa `aks), and equality in predication with the name. So whenever a definition is established, the name applies; and whenever the name applies, the definition obtains. By the second respect we mean equality in meaning, namely that it indicates the full reality of the essence, not lacking anything from it. For many a distinguished essential [attribute] whose some differentiae are omitted does not bring to mind a comprehensible form of the defined that corresponds to the fullness of its essence. And this is what definitions require, and we have mentioned its aspect.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage explains the method of composing a definition (tarkib). The author responds to the question of how a definition is acquired if not by demonstration. The method involves: (1) taking concrete individuals of the thing to be defined (e.g., a specific substance) to avoid division, (2) determining which of the ten categories it belongs to, (3) collecting all essential predicates (al-mahmulat al-muqawwima) that are in that genus, ignoring accidents and necessary consequences, (4) removing redundant predicates, (5) retaining only the nearest genus (i.e., the closest broader category), (6) adding the differentia (fasl) to the genus. The resulting definition must satisfy two conditions: (a) coextensiveness (al-tard wa al-`aks): the definition and the name are mutually convertible—whenever the definition holds, the name applies, and vice versa; (b) equality in meaning (al-musawa fi al-ma`na): the definition must convey the complete essence without omission. The author illustrates that omitting some differentiae from an essential attribute fails to produce a proper mental image of the defined. This method ensures the definition is both extensionally and intensionally accurate.

Key Terms
التركيب
الطرد والعكس
المساواة في المعنى
المحمولات المقومة
المحدود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only coextensiveness (الطرد والعكس)
B) Only equality in meaning (المساواة في المعنى)
C) Both coextensiveness and equality in meaning
D) The definition must be shorter than the name

Key Takeaway
To compose a valid definition, one must (1) eliminate redundant essential predicates, (2) add the differentia, and (3) ensure the result is coextensive and fully conveys the essence.

The Infinite Regress Objection to Demonstrative Definition
Author presents first case against definition via demonstration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the infinite regress argument against proving a definition by demonstration and identify the logical dilemma.

Core Idea
If a definition needs proof, then either the proof itself needs another definition ad infinitum, or we already know the definition without proof.

The author argues that definition cannot be attained through demonstration (burhan). The first case he examines is when the middle term of a syllogism is itself a definition. He shows that this leads to an infinite regress or forces us to admit that definition can be known without a middle term. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Find where the author states that the middle term is taken as a definition for the minor term. This is the starting point of the first objection.
The phrase 'الأوسط بما عرف كونه حدا للأصغر'
2
Follow the regress
If the middle term is known to be a definition through another definition, that second definition would itself require proof, leading to an infinite chain.
3
Recognize the alternative
The author points out that if at some point a definition is known without a middle term, then the original definition could also be known without a middle term, making the demonstration redundant.
The phrase 'فليعرف الأول بلا وسط'
4
Formulate the dilemma
The argument presents a dilemma: either infinite regress (impossible) or the possibility of knowing a definition without demonstration, which undermines the need for demonstration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفن الأول : في قوانين الحدود
في اللفظ وإن كان مغايراً له في الحقيقة، لم يكن حدا للأصغر. الثاني: أن الأوسط بما عرف كونه حدا للأصغر، فإن عرف بحد آخر فالسؤال قائم في ذلك الآخر، وذلك إما أن يتسلسل إلى غير نهاية وهو محال وإما أن يعرف بلا وسط فليعرف الأول بلا وسط إذا أمكن معرفة الحدّ بغير وسط.
الحالة الثانية : أن لا يكون الأوسط حداً للأصغر بل كان رسماً أو خاصة وهو باطل من وجهين: أحدهما أن ما ليس بحد ولا هو ذاتي مقوم كيف صار أعرف من الذاتي المقوم، وكيف يتصوّر أن تعرف من الإنسان أنه ضحاك أو ماش ولا يعرف جسم وحيوان والثاني : أن الأكبر بهذا الأوسط إن كان محمولاً مطلقاً وليس بحد فليس يلزم منه إلَّا كونه محمولاً للأصغر، ولا يلزمه كونه حدا، وإن كان حدا فهو محال إذ حدّ الخاصية والعَرَض لا يكون حدّ موضوع الخاصية والعرض، فليس حدّ الضاحك هو بعينه حدّ الإنسان، وإن قيل : إنه محمول على الأوسط على موضوعه، فهذه مصادرة على المطلوب، فقد تبيّن أن الحد لا يكتسب بالبرهان.
The first art: On the laws of definitions. In the utterance even if it is different from it in reality, it is not a definition for the minor. Second: The middle term by what is known to be a definition for the minor, if it is known by another definition then the question remains for that other, and that either leads to infinite regress which is impossible, or it is known without a middle term, so let the first be known without a middle term if it is possible to know the definition without a middle term. The second case: That the middle term is not a definition for the minor but rather a rasam (description) or special property (khassa), and it is invalid from two aspects: One: that which is not a definition nor a constitutive essential (dhati muqawwim), how does it become more known than the constitutive essential, and how can it be imagined that one knows of man that he is 'laughing' or 'walking' but does not know body and animal? The second: that the major through this middle term, if it is predicated absolutely and is not a definition, then nothing follows from it except that it is predicated of the minor, and it does not necessitate that it is a definition; and if it is a definition, then it is impossible because the definition of a property or accident is not the definition of the subject of the property or accident, so the definition of 'laughing' is not exactly the definition of man. And if it is said: it is predicated of the middle term upon its subject, then this is a petition of what is desired (musadara 'ala al-matlub). So it has become clear that the definition is not acquired through demonstration.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a critical argument showing that definition cannot be acquired through demonstration (burhan). The author presents two cases. First, if the middle term in a demonstration is a definition for the minor term, then one must explain how we know it is a definition, leading to either infinite regress or the need to know the definition without a middle term. Second, if the middle term is not a definition but a description (rasm) or property (khassa), then it is either not constitutive and thus cannot be more known than the essence, or if it is taken as a definition, it would define a property, not the subject, leading to a petition of the question. The conclusion is that definitions must be known through composition (tarkib), not demonstration. For example, one cannot use a syllogism to prove that man is a rational animal without already knowing what man is.

Key Terms
الحد
الأوسط
البرهان
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first case in the passage, what happens if the middle term is known as a definition through another definition?
A) The syllogism becomes invalid.
B) It leads to infinite regress or the need to know a definition without a middle term.
C) The middle term must be a property.
D) The definition becomes self-evident.

Key Takeaway
Definition cannot be proven by demonstration because it would require an infinite regress of definitions or a circular admission that definition can be known without proof.

Why a Description Cannot Serve as a Definition in Demonstration
Author presents second case against definition via demonstration using description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a genuine definition (hadd) and a description (rasm) in a syllogistic context, and explain why a description cannot prove a definition.

Core Idea
A property like 'laughing' cannot define 'man', because it is not constitutive and would lead to circularity.

The author presents a second case: the middle term in a demonstration is not a definition but a description (rasm) or special property (khassa). He gives two powerful objections. First, how can a non-essential property be more known than the essence? Second, if the conclusion is a definition, it would define the property, not the subject, or else the argument becomes circular. This lesson unpacks these objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second scenario
Find where the author states that the middle term is a rasm or khassa, not a hadd.
The phrase 'لا يكون الأوسط حداً للأصغر بل كان رسماً أو خاصة'
2
Analyze the first objection
The author asks: how can a non-essential property (e.g., laughing) be more known than the essential components (e.g., body and animal)? This relies on the principle that definition should be from what is better known.
The rhetorical question about 'ضحاك أو ماش' vs 'جسم وحيوان'
3
Analyze the second objection
If the conclusion predicates a definition (e.g., 'rational animal') via a middle term that is a property, either the conclusion is not a definition of the subject or the definition is actually of the property, leading to musadara (petitio principii).
The argument that 'حد الخاصية والعرض لا يكون حد موضوع الخاصية والعرض'
4
Understand the final verdict
The author concludes that definition cannot be acquired through demonstration, because any attempt either falls into infinite regress or confuses definition with description.
The final sentence 'فقد تبيّن أن الحد لا يكتسب بالبرهان'

Source Text

The second: that the major through this middle term, if it is predicated absolutely and is not a definition, then nothing follows from it except that it is predicated of the minor, and it does not necessitate that it is a definition; and if it is a definition, then it is impossible because the definition of a property or accident is not the definition of the subject of the property or accident, so the definition of 'laughing' is not exactly the definition of man. Six Common Errors in Genus Placement
Author lists six ways the genus can be misused in definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the six common errors where the genus is incorrectly replaced in a definition.

Core Idea
The genus is not matter, parts, species, differentia, hyle, or disposition.

A sound definition requires placing the correct genus. The author identifies six errors where something else is mistakenly put in its place. Learning these errors sharpens your ability to evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the six error types
The author lists six substitutions: differentia, matter, hyle, parts, disposition, and species. Read each example carefully.
2
For each error, extract the incorrect genus
Identify which term is wrongly taken as the genus and why it does not work. For example, in 'iron that cuts', iron is matter, not genus.
3
Identify the correct genus
Think of what the proper genus should be. For sword, the genus is 'weapon' or 'tool', not 'iron'.
4
Apply to new examples
Practice recognising the error in examples from Islamic texts, such as defining 'salah' as 'bowing and prostrating' (matter vs. genus).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل السادس : مثارات الغلط في الحدود وهي ثلاثة : أحدها في الجنس، والآخر في الفصل، والثالث مشترك. المثار الأول : الجنس وهو من وجوه فمنها أن يوضع الفصل بدل الجنس فيقال في العشق إنه إفراط المحبة، وإنما هو المحبة المفرطة فالمحبة جنس والإفراط فصل ومنها أن توضع المادة مكان الجنس كقولك للسيف: إنه حديد يقطع، وللكرسي : إنه خشب يجلس عليه. ومنها أن تؤخذ الهيولى مكان الجنس كقولنا للرماد : إنه خشب محترق، فإنه ليس خشباً في الحال بل كان خشباً بخلاف الخشب من السرير فإنه موجود فيه على أنه مادة، وليس موجوداً في الرماد، ولكن كان فصار شيئاً آخر بتبدّل صورته الذاتية، وهو الذي أردنا بالهيولى، ولك أن تعبّر عنه بعبارة أخرى إن استبشعت هذه العبارة ومنها أن تُؤخذ الأجزاء بدل الجنس في حد العشرة : أنه خمسة وخمسة أو ستة وأربعة أو ثلاثة وسبعة وأمثالها، وليس كذلك قولنا في الحيوان : إنه جسم ونفس لأن كون الجسم نفساً ما يرجع إلى فصل ذاتي له فإن النفس صورة وكمال للجسم ولا كالخمسة للخمسة الأخرى. ومنها أن تُوضع الملكة مكان القوة كقولنا : العفيف هو القوي على اجتناب اللذات الشهوانية، وليس كذلك إذ الفاجر أيضاً يقوى ولكنه يفعل، ولكن يكون ترك اللذات للعفيف بالملكة الراسخة وللفاجر بالقوة. وقد تشتبه الملكة بالقوة، وكقولك : إن القادر على الظلم هو الذي من شأنه وطباعه النزوع إلى انتزاع ما ليس له من يد غيره، فقد وضع الملكة مكان القوة لأن القادر على الظلم قد يكون عادلاً لا ينزع طبعه إلى الظلم. ومنها أن يوضع النوع بدل الجنس فيقال: الشرّ هو ظلم الناس، والظلم أحد أنواع الشرّ والشرّ جنس عام يتناول غير الظلم.
The sixth chapter: Occasions of error in definitions. They are three: one in the genus, another in the differentia, and a third common. The first occasion: the genus, and it has several aspects. Among them: that the differentia is put in place of the genus, as when it is said of love that it is excess of affection, whereas it is excessive affection, so affection is the genus and excess is the differentia. Among them: that the matter is put in place of the genus, as your saying of the sword that it is iron that cuts, and of the chair that it is wood that is sat upon. Among them: that the hyle (material substrate) is taken in place of the genus, as our saying of ashes that it is burnt wood, for it is not wood in the present state but was wood, unlike the wood of the bed which exists in it as matter, and it does not exist in ashes, but it was and became something else by the change of its essential form, and that is what we meant by hyle, and you may express it with another phrase if this phrase is considered ugly. Among them: that the parts are taken in place of the genus in the definition of ten: that it is five and five, or six and four, or three and seven and the like. That is not like our saying of animal that it is a body and a soul, because the soul being a body goes back to an essential differentia for it, for the soul is form and perfection for the body, not like five for the other five. Among them: that disposition (malaka) is put in place of power (quwwa), as our saying: the chaste person is the one who is powerful at avoiding sensual pleasures, but that is not so because the immoral person also is powerful but he does it, but avoidance of pleasures for the chaste is by a rooted disposition, and for the immoral by power. And disposition may be confused with power, and like your saying: the one capable of injustice is the one whose habit and nature is to tend to take what is not his from the hand of another, thus he put disposition in place of power because the one capable of injustice may be just, his nature not tending to injustice. Among them: that the species is put in place of the genus, as when it is said: evil is oppression of people, while oppression is one of the types of evil, and evil is a general genus that includes other than oppression.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage enumerates errors in definitions where the genus is incorrectly replaced. Six sub-errors are given: (1) substituting the differentia for the genus (e.g., defining love as 'excess of affection' when it should be 'excessive affection'); (2) substituting matter for genus (e.g., 'iron that cuts' for sword); (3) substituting hyle (material substrate) for genus (e.g., 'burnt wood' for ashes, which is not currently wood); (4) substituting parts for genus (e.g., defining ten as 'five and five' instead of a number); (5) substituting disposition (malaka) for power (quwwa) (e.g., defining the chaste as 'powerful at avoiding pleasures' while the immoral also has power); (6) substituting species for genus (e.g., defining evil as 'oppression' which is only one species). Each error is illustrated with an example from everyday language or common reasoning.

الفصل
المادة
الهيولى
الأجزاء
الملكة
القوة
النوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which error occurs when defining a sword as 'iron that cuts'?
A) Putting differentia in place of genus
B) Putting matter in place of genus
C) Putting species in place of genus
D) Putting parts in place of genus

Key Takeaway
A definition fails if the genus is replaced by matter, parts, species, differentia, hyle, or disposition instead of the true categorical genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Constructing a Proper Definition: The Method of Hadd
Step-by-step method for constructing a proper definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the step-by-step method for constructing a correct definition (hadd) by identifying the nearest genus and essential differentiae, and verifying predication equality.

Core Idea
A complete definition requires the nearest genus and all essential differentiae, nothing more, nothing less.

Defining terms correctly is essential in all Islamic sciences, from usul al-fiqh to kalam. In this passage, the author lays out the exact method for constructing a proper definition (hadd). You will learn how to identify the genus, separate by differentia, and check for completeness — a skill that prevents ambiguity in scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nearest genus
Find the broad category that contains the essential attributes common to all members of the species. In the example, 'drink' is the genus for a specific intoxicating beverage.
2
Separate by an essential differentia
Choose a distinguishing attribute that is essential (ذاتي), not accidental. The example uses 'intoxicating' to separate this drink from other drinks.
3
Verify predication equality
Check that the definition (genus + differentia) applies to all and only the things called by that name. This is 'equal in both sides of predication' (يساوي الاسم في طرفي الحمل).
4
Include all essential differentiae
If the definition misses an essential differentia without which the essence is incomplete, add it. For example, 'body possessing a sentient soul' for animal is not enough; 'moving by will' is also essential.
5
Confirm the definition is final
The author states that this is the only correct method. After including all essential differentiae, the definition is complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجنس الأقرب المتضمن لجميع الذاتيات العامة وهو شراب، فنراه مساوياً لغيره من الأشربة فتفصله عنه بفصل ذاتي لا عرضي كقولنا : مسكر يحفظ في الدنّ أو مثله، فيجتمع لنا شراب مسكر فتنظر هل يساوي الاسم في طرفي الحمل، فإن ساواه فتنظر هل تركنا فصلاً آخر ذاتياً لا تتم ذاته إلا به ، فإن وجد معنا ضممناه إليه كما إذا وجدنا في حدّ الحيوان أنه جسم ذو نفس حسّاس، وهو يساوي الاسم في الحمل، ولكن ثم فصل آخر ذاتي وهو المتحرك بالإرادة فينبغي أن تضيفه إليه ؛ فهذا طريق تحصيل الحدود لا طريق سواه.
The nearest genus that includes all universal essences, and it is 'drink', so we find it equal to other drinks, then we separate it by an essential differentia, not accidental, like saying 'an intoxicant stored in a jar or the like', so we have 'intoxicating drink'. Then we check whether it equals the name in both sides of predication. If it equals, then we check whether we have left out another essential differentia without which its essence is not complete. If we find it, we add it to it, as we find in the definition of animal that it is a body possessing a sentient soul, and it equals the name in predication, but there is another essential differentia, which is 'moving by will', so it should be added to it. This is the way to obtain definitions, no other way.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage provides the method for constructing a definition (hadd). The author uses the example of defining a specific intoxicating beverage. First, identify the nearest genus (الجنس الأقرب) that includes all the universal essential attributes. In the example, the genus is 'drink' (شراب). Then, differentiate it from other drinks by an essential differentia (فصل ذاتي), not an accidental one. The differentia here is 'intoxicating' (مسكر). Next, verify that the definition (genus + differentia) exactly equals the defined term in predication (يساوي الاسم في طرفي الحمل). If it does, check whether another essential differentia is missing without which the essence is incomplete. If found, add it, as in the definition of animal: 'body possessing a sentient soul' is not enough; 'moving by will' is also essential. The passage concludes that this is the only correct method for obtaining definitions.

Key Terms
الجنس الأقرب
فصل ذاتي
المحمل

Key Takeaway
A correct definition requires the nearest genus plus all essential differentiae, verified by predication equality.

Six Errors in Substituting the Genus
Author enumerates common mistakes where genus is replaced by differentia, matter, material, parts, disposition, or species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify six common mistakes where the genus is replaced by something else in a definition and correct each error.

Core Idea
The genus is the essential category; substituting matter, parts, or species destroys the definition.

The author enumerates six distinct errors that occur when defining terms: placing differentia, matter, prime matter, parts, disposition, or species in the place of genus. Each error leads to a defective definition that either fails to include all members or includes non-members. Understanding these pitfalls is crucial for constructing sound definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genuine genus and differentia
For any definiendum, determine its true genus (the essential category) and differentia (the distinguishing feature). In the error of 'excessive love', the genus is 'love' and the differentia is 'excessive', but the definition incorrectly presents 'excess' as the genus.
2
Spot matter/hayula substitution vs genus
Matter (madda) is the physical substance, not the logical genus. For example, calling a sword 'iron that cuts' mistakes 'iron' (matter) for the genus. Similarly, prime matter (hayula) refers to a prior state, not the current genus – as in 'ashes are burnt wood'.
3
Spot parts substitution vs genus
Parts are components, not the genus. Defining ten as 'five and five' lists parts, not the genus (which would be 'number'). This is different from 'animal is body and soul', where 'body and soul' refers to an essential differentia.
4
Spot disposition/power confusion
Disposition (malaka) is a stable habit, while power (quwwa) is mere capacity. Saying 'the chaste is strong enough to abstain' uses 'strong' as genus, but it should be 'disposition'. The immoral also has the power to abstain but lacks the disposition.
5
Spot species substitution vs genus
Species is narrower than genus; using species as genus excludes other species. Defining 'evil' as 'oppression' restricts it to one type, while evil includes many other forms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثار الأول : الجنس وهو من وجوه فمنها أن يوضع الفصل بدل الجنس فيقال في العشق إنه إفراط المحبة، وإنما هو المحبة المفرطة فالمحبة جنس والإفراط فصل ومنها أن توضع المادة مكان الجنس كقولك للسيف: إنه حديد يقطع، وللكرسي : إنه خشب يجلس عليه. ومنها أن تؤخذ الهيولى مكان الجنس كقولنا للرماد : إنه خشب محترق، فإنه ليس خشباً في الحال بل كان خشباً بخلاف الخشب من السرير فإنه موجود فيه على أنه مادة، وليس موجوداً في الرماد، ولكن كان فصار شيئاً آخر بتبدّل صورته الذاتية، وهو الذي أردنا بالهيولى، ولك أن تعبّر عنه بعبارة أخرى إن استبشعت هذه العبارة ومنها أن تُؤخذ الأجزاء بدل الجنس في حد العشرة : أنه خمسة أنه خمسة وخمسة أو ستة وأربعة أو ثلاثة وسبعة وأمثالها، وليس كذلك قولنا في الحيوان : إنه جسم ونفس لأن كون الجسم نفساً ما يرجع إلى فصل ذاتي ،له فإن النفس صورة وكمال للجسم ولا كالخمسة للخمسة الأخرى. ومنها أن تُوضع الملكة مكان القوة كقولنا : العفيف هو القوي على اجتناب اللذات الشهوانية، وليس كذلك إذ الفاجر أيضاً يقوى ولكنه يفعل، ولكن يكون ترك اللذات للعفيف بالملكة الراسخة وللفاجر بالقوة. وقد تشتبه الملكة بالقوة، وكقولك : إن القادر على الظلم هو الذي من شأنه وطباعه النزوع إلى انتزاع ما ليس له من يد غيره، فقد وضع الملكة مكان القوة لأن القادر على الظلم قد يكون عادلاً لا ينزع طبعه إلى الظلم. ومنها أن يوضع النوع بدل الجنس فيقال: الشرّ هو ظلم الناس، والظلم أحد أنواع الشرّ والشرّ جنس عام يتناول غير الظلم.
The first source: the genus, and it has aspects. Among them is that the differentia is placed in the position of the genus, as one says in defining love that it is 'excess of love', whereas it is 'excessive love'; so 'love' is the genus and 'excess' is the differentia. Among them is that matter is placed in place of the genus, like saying of a sword that it is 'iron that cuts', and of a chair that it is 'wood to sit on'. Among them is that prime matter (hayula) is taken as the genus, like saying of ashes that they are 'burnt wood', but they are not wood currently, they were wood; unlike wood of a bed which exists in it as matter, and it does not exist in ashes, but it was and became something else by change of its essential form. This is what we mean by hayula. You may express it differently if you dislike this expression. Among them is that parts are taken instead of the genus in the definition of ten: that it is 'five and five' or 'six and four' or 'three and seven' and the like. This is not like our saying of animal that it is 'body and soul', because being a body and soul refers to an essential differentia, for the soul is a form and perfection for the body, not like the five for the other five. Among them is that disposition (malaka) is placed in place of power (quwwa), like saying: 'the chaste is the one who is strong enough to abstain from sensual pleasures', but it is not so, for the immoral also has strength but he does it; rather abstinence for the chaste is due to established disposition, and for the immoral it is due to power. And disposition may be confused with power, and like your saying: 'the one capable of injustice is the one whose nature and temperament incline to take what is not his from another's hand', so you have placed disposition in place of power, because the one capable of injustice may be just, his nature not inclined to injustice. Among them is that the species is placed in place of the genus, like saying 'evil is oppressing people', whereas oppression is one of the types of evil, and evil is a general genus that encompasses other than oppression.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage details the first source of error in definitions, which concerns the genus (الجنس). It lists several common mistakes: (1) Placing the differentia in the position of the genus, e.g., defining love as 'excess of love' when the correct genus is 'love' and the differentia is 'excess'. (2) Placing matter (مادة) instead of genus, like defining a sword as 'iron that cuts'—iron is the matter, not the genus. (3) Placing prime matter (هيولى) instead of genus, like calling ashes 'burnt wood'—ashes are no longer wood. (4) Taking parts instead of genus, like defining ten as 'five and five'—this is not a proper genus. (5) Placing disposition (ملكة) instead of power (قوة), e.g., defining the chaste as 'strong to abstain'—the chaste has a stable disposition, not mere power. (6) Placing the species instead of genus, like defining evil as 'oppression'—evil is broader. Each error leads to an incorrect definition.

Key Terms
مادة
هيولى
ملكة
قوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A correct definition must have the genus as the essential category; any substitution with differentia, matter, parts, disposition, or species yields a defective definition.

The Second Source of Error: Misplacing the Differentia
Brief warning about replacing differentia with non-essential attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a definition incorrectly uses genus, property, necessary concomitant, or accidental attribute in place of the differentia.

Core Idea
The differentia must be essential; substitutes like genus, property, or accident produce flawed definitions.

In this lesson, we examine the second major source of error in definitions: the differentia (الفصل) being replaced by something else. The author lists four common impostors: the genus (جنس), a property (خاصة), a necessary concomitant (لازم), or an accidental attribute (عرضي). This error is frequent and difficult to guard against, so we must learn to detect it. By recognizing these impostors, you will strengthen your ability to evaluate definitions critically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined in the definition. For example, if the definition is 'Ijtihad is exerting effort to derive a ruling', the definiendum is 'ijtihad'.
2
Extract the purported differentia
Look at the part of the definition that is supposed to distinguish the definiendum from other things in its genus. In the ijtihad example, the differentia would be 'exerting effort to derive a ruling'.
3
Classify the impostor
Determine whether the purported differentia is actually a genus, a property (khassa), a necessary concomitant (lazim), or an accidental attribute ('aradi). Check its characteristics: genus is a broader category; property is unique but non-essential; necessary concomitant necessarily accompanies the essence but is not part of it; accidental may or may not be present.
Use the key terms provided for definitions of these impostors.
4
Assess correctness
If the purported differentia falls into any of the four impostor categories, the definition is flawed. A correct differentia must be essential to the definiendum. For example, defining 'ijtihad' as 'effort' (genus) without specifying 'legal ruling derivation' would be incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفن الأول : في قوانين الحدود المثار الثاني من جهة الفصل، وذلك بأن يُوضع ما هو جنس مكان الفصل، أو ما هو خاصة أو لازم أو عَرَضي مكان الفصل وكثيراً ما يتفق ذلك والاحتراز عنه عَسِرٌ جداً.
The first art: on the rules of definitions. The second source is regarding the differentia, and that is by placing what is a genus in the place of the differentia, or what is a property (khassa), or necessary concomitant (lazim), or accidental ('aradi) in the place of the differentia. This happens often and guarding against it is very difficult.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This brief passage introduces the second source of error, which concerns the differentia (الفصل). It warns that the differentia can be mistakenly replaced with the genus (جنس), or with a property (خاصة), a necessary concomitant (لازم), or an accidental attribute (عرضي). The author notes that such errors are common and avoiding them is very difficult.

Key Terms

لازم
عرضي

C) Necessary concomitant
D) Species

Key Takeaway
In definitions, the differentia must be essential; replacing it with genus, property, necessary concomitant, or accidental attribute leads to error.

First Error: Defining by What is More Obscure
Error: defining by what is more obscure - the example of fire and soul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify definitions that use terms more obscure than the definiendum and construct a valid alternative.

Core Idea
Defining the unknown by the more unknown is circular obscurity.

One of the most common errors in definition is to define a thing by something even less known. The author gives the example of defining fire as 'a body similar to the soul,' where the soul is more obscure. This violates the principle that a definition must clarify, not further obscure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
What is being defined? In the example, fire (النار).
2
Extract the genus and differentia
Genus: 'body' (جسم); differentia: 'similar to the soul' (شبيه بالنفس). Ask: does the differentia add clarity?
3
Compare obscurity levels
Is the differentia more or less known than the definiendum? The author asserts the soul (النفس) is more obscure than fire. Check if the definition actually makes the concept clearer.
4
Evaluate the definition's validity
A valid definition must illuminate; if it relies on something more obscure, it fails. Conclude that this definition is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثار الثالث : ما هو مشترك وهو على وجوه فمنها أن يعرف الشيء بما هو أخفى منه كمن يحدّ النار بأنه جسم شبيه بالنفس والنفس أخفى من النار، أو يحدّه بما هو مثله في المعرفة كتحديد الضدّ بالضد مثل قولك : الزوج ما ليس بفرد، ثم تقول : الفرد ما ليس بزوج، أو تقول : الزوج ما يزيد على الفرد بواحد، ثم تقول: الفرد ما ينقص عن الزوج بواحد، وكذا إذا أخذ المضاف في حد المضاف، فتقول: العلم ما يكون الذات عالماً. به ثم تقول : العالم من قام به العلم والمتضايفان يُعلمان معاً، ولا يعلم أحدهما بالآخر بل مع الآخر. فمن جهل العلم جهل العالم، ومن جهل الأب جهل الابن فمن القبيح أن يقال للسائل الذي يقول : ما الأب من له ابن فإنه يقول : لو عرفت الابن لعرفت الأب بل ينغي يقال : الأب حيوان يوجد آخر من نوعه من نطفته من حيث هو كذلك، فلا يكون فيه تعريف الشيء بنفسه ولا حوالته على ما مثله هو في الجهالة. ومنها أن يعرف الشيء بنفسه أو بما هو متأخر عنه في المعرفة كقولك للشمس : كوكب يطلع نهاراً، ولا يمكن تعريف النهار إلا بالشمس، فإن معناه زمان طلوع الشمس فهو تابع للشمس فكيف يعرف؟ وكقولك في الكيفية : إن الكيفية ما بها تقع المشابهة وخلافها، ولا يمكن تعريف المشابهة إلا بأنها اتفاق في الكيفية، وربما يخالف المساواة فإنها اتفاق في الكمية وتخالف المشاكلة فإنها اتفاق في النوع؛ فهذا وأمثاله مما يجب مراقبته في الحدود حتى لا يتطرّق إليه الخطأ بإغفاله، وأمثلة هذا مما يخرج عن الحصر، وفيما ذكرنا تنبيه على الجنس.
The third source: that which is common, and it has aspects. Among them is that a thing is defined by what is more obscure than it, like one defining fire as 'a body similar to the soul' while the soul is more obscure than fire. Or defining it by what is equal in knowledge, like defining the opposite by the opposite, such as saying 'the even is what is not odd', then saying 'the odd is what is not even'; or saying 'the even is what exceeds the odd by one', then saying 'the odd is what is less than the even by one'. And similarly if one takes the relative in the definition of the relative, as you say 'knowledge is that by which the essence is knowing', then say 'the knower is the one in whom knowledge resides'. The two relatives are known together, not one by the other but with the other. So whoever is ignorant of knowledge is ignorant of the knower, and whoever is ignorant of the father is ignorant of the son. Thus it is ugly to say to the questioner who says 'What is the father?' to answer 'He who has a son', for he would say 'If I knew the son I would know the father'; rather one should say 'The father is an animal that produces another of its kind from his sperm, insofar as he is such.' So there is no definition of a thing by itself nor a reference to what is equally ignorant. Among them is that a thing is defined by itself or by what is posterior to it in knowledge, like saying of the sun 'a planet that rises in the daytime', but daytime cannot be defined except by the sun, for its meaning is the time of sunrise, so it is dependent on the sun, so how can it be defined? And like your saying of quality: 'quality is that by which similarity and its opposite occur', but similarity cannot be defined except as agreement in quality. Perhaps it differs from equality, which is agreement in quantity, and differs from similarity (mushakala), which is agreement in species. So these and their like must be watched in definitions so that error does not arise from neglecting them. Examples of this are beyond count, and in what we have mentioned is a reminder of the genus.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage covers the third source of error, which is common to both genus and differentia. It lists several types: (1) Defining something by what is more obscure than it, e.g., defining fire as 'a body similar to the soul'. (2) Defining by what is equally unknown, e.g., defining opposites by each other (even/odd) without a proper genus, or defining relatives by each other (knowledge/knower). (3) Defining a thing by itself or by something posterior in knowledge, e.g., defining the sun as 'a planet that rises in daytime', but daytime is defined by the sun, creating circularity. Another example: defining quality by similarity, but similarity is defined by quality. The author stresses that such errors must be vigilantly avoided.

Key Terms
الضد (al-didd): The opposite; defining something by its opposite is an error if it leads to circularity.
المضاف (al-mudaf): The relative term; relatives are known together and cannot be defined separately by each other.
المشابهة (al-mushabaha): Similarity; used in the definition of quality but itself defined by quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of defining a thing by something more obscure?
A) Defining fire as 'a body similar to the soul'
B) Defining even as 'what is not odd'
C) Defining father as 'he who has a son'
D) Defining the sun as 'a planet that rises in daytime'

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must not use terms that are less known than the definiendum.

?

Second Error: Circular Definitions via Opposites and Relatives
Error: circular definitions via opposites and relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to detect circular definitions that use opposites or relatives and offer a proper non-circular definition.

Core Idea
Opposites and relatives are co-dependent; using one to define the other yields no knowledge.

Another common error is defining a term by its opposite or by a relative term that is known only together with the definiendum. The author illustrates with examples: defining 'even' as 'not odd' and then 'odd' as 'not even', or defining 'knowledge' by 'knower' and vice versa. This creates a vicious circle that fails to provide independent understanding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pair of opposites or relatives
In the example, even (زوج) and odd (فرد) are opposites. Also, knowledge (علم) and knower (عالم) are relatives.
2
Check the definitions for mutual dependence
Does each definition rely on the other? For even/odd, 'even is what is not odd' and 'odd is what is not even' – each uses the other, so they are mutually dependent.
3
Determine if the definition provides new information
A person ignorant of both terms gains no knowledge from such definitions. The circle needs to be broken by introducing an independent genus or differentia.
4
Propose a corrected definition
For even, a proper definition could be 'a number that is divisible by two' (genus: number, differentia: divisible by two). This does not rely on odd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثار الثالث : ما هو مشترك وهو على وجوه فمنها أن يعرف الشيء بما هو أخفى منه كمن يحدّ النار بأنه جسم شبيه بالنفس والنفس أخفى من النار، أو يحدّه بما هو مثله في المعرفة كتحديد الضدّ بالضد مثل قولك : الزوج ما ليس بفرد، ثم تقول : الفرد ما ليس بزوج، أو تقول : الزوج ما يزيد على الفرد بواحد، ثم تقول: الفرد ما ينقص عن الزوج بواحد، وكذا إذا أخذ المضاف في حد المضاف، فتقول: العلم ما يكون الذات عالماً. به ثم تقول : العالم من قام به العلم والمتضايفان يُعلمان معاً، ولا يعلم أحدهما بالآخر بل مع الآخر. فمن جهل العلم جهل العالم، ومن جهل الأب جهل الابن فمن القبيح أن يقال للسائل الذي يقول : ما الأب من له ابن فإنه يقول : لو عرفت الابن لعرفت الأب بل ينغي يقال : الأب حيوان يوجد آخر من نوعه من نطفته من حيث هو كذلك، فلا يكون فيه تعريف الشيء بنفسه ولا حوالته على ما مثله هو في الجهالة. ومنها أن يعرف الشيء بنفسه أو بما هو متأخر عنه في المعرفة كقولك للشمس : كوكب يطلع نهاراً، ولا يمكن تعريف النهار إلا بالشمس، فإن معناه زمان طلوع الشمس فهو تابع للشمس فكيف يعرف؟ وكقولك في الكيفية : إن الكيفية ما بها تقع المشابهة وخلافها، ولا يمكن تعريف المشابهة إلا بأنها اتفاق في الكيفية، وربما يخالف المساواة فإنها اتفاق في الكمية وتخالف المشاكلة فإنها اتفاق في النوع؛ فهذا وأمثاله مما يجب مراقبته في الحدود حتى لا يتطرّق إليه الخطأ بإغفاله، وأمثلة هذا مما يخرج عن الحصر، وفيما ذكرنا تنبيه على الجنس.
The third source: that which is common, and it has aspects. Among them is that a thing is defined by what is more obscure than it, like one defining fire as 'a body similar to the soul' while the soul is more obscure than fire. Or defining it by what is equal in knowledge, like defining the opposite by the opposite, such as saying 'the even is what is not odd', then saying 'the odd is what is not even'; or saying 'the even is what exceeds the odd by one', then saying 'the odd is what is less than the even by one'. And similarly if one takes the relative in the definition of the relative, as you say 'knowledge is that by which the essence is knowing', then say 'the knower is the one in whom knowledge resides'. The two relatives are known together, not one by the other but with the other. So whoever is ignorant of knowledge is ignorant of the knower, and whoever is ignorant of the father is ignorant of the son. Thus it is ugly to say to the questioner who says 'What is the father?' to answer 'He who has a son', for he would say 'If I knew the son I would know the father'; rather one should say 'The father is an animal that produces another of its kind from his sperm, insofar as he is such.' So there is no definition of a thing by itself nor a reference to what is equally ignorant. Among them is that a thing is defined by itself or by what is posterior to it in knowledge, like saying of the sun 'a planet that rises in the daytime', but daytime cannot be defined except by the sun, for its meaning is the time of sunrise, so it is dependent on the sun, so how can it be defined? And like your saying of quality: 'quality is that by which similarity and its opposite occur', but similarity cannot be defined except as agreement in quality. Perhaps it differs from equality, which is agreement in quantity, and differs from similarity (mushakala), which is agreement in species. So these and their like must be watched in definitions so that error does not arise from neglecting them. Examples of this are beyond count, and in what we have mentioned is a reminder of the genus.
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage covers the third source of error, which is common to both genus and differentia. It lists several types: (1) Defining something by what is more obscure than it, e.g., defining fire as 'a body similar to the soul'. (2) Defining by what is equally unknown, e.g., defining opposites by each other (even/odd) without a proper genus, or defining relatives by each other (knowledge/knower). (3) Defining a thing by itself or by something posterior in knowledge, e.g., defining the sun as 'a planet that rises in daytime', but daytime is defined by the sun, creating circularity. Another example: defining quality by similarity, but similarity is defined by quality. The author stresses that such errors must be vigilantly avoided.

Key Terms
الضد
المضاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a circular definition?
A) Fire is a body similar to the soul.
B) Even is what is not odd.
C) The sun is a planet that rises in daytime.
D) Quality is that by which similarity occurs.

Key Takeaway
A definition must not rely on the term it defines or a co-dependent opposite or relative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the definition: 'Valid contract is that which is not invalid.' Is this a valid definition? Explain why or why not, and propose a corrected definition using genus and differentia from Islamic contract law.

Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
6 min
Third Error: Self-Referential and Posterior Definitions
Error: self-referential and posterior definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify definitions that are self-referential or use terms posterior to the definiendum and correct them.

Core Idea
A definition must not presuppose knowledge of the thing defined.

The third error includes defining a thing by itself or by something that is defined in terms of the thing. The author gives the sun/daytime example: defining the sun as 'a planet that rises in daytime' fails because daytime is defined by the sun. Similarly, defining quality by similarity fails because similarity is defined by quality. Such definitions are circular and should be avoided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum and the defining phrase
For sun (الشمس): 'a planet that rises in daytime'. For quality (الكيفية): 'that by which similarity occurs'.
2
Check if the defining phrase itself depends on the definiendum
Daytime (النهار) is defined as 'time of sunrise', which uses the concept of sun. So defining sun by daytime is circular. Similarly, similarity (المشابهة) is defined as 'agreement in quality', so defining quality by similarity is circular.
3
Determine the direction of dependence
The definiendum should be more basic than the defining terms. Here, sun is prior to daytime, and quality is prior to similarity. Using the posterior to define the prior is erroneous.
4
Propose a valid alternative
For sun, define it by its intrinsic properties: 'a luminous celestial body around which the earth orbits' (though this is modern). For quality, define it as 'an attribute that distinguishes objects' or using the Aristotelian categories.

Key Terms
المشابهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following defines a thing by itself or by something posterior?
A) Fire is a body similar to the soul.
B) Even is what is not odd.
C) Daytime is the time of sunrise; sunrise is when the sun appears at daytime.
D) Father is he who has a son.

Key Takeaway
A definition must not depend on the very term it defines or on terms that presuppose it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Check the following definition: 'Day is the time when the sun is visible.' Is this definition self-referential? Explain. Then suggest a better definition.
